class="css-6n7j50"><button aria-expanded="false" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="More sharing options" class="css-16ogagc" data-testid=""><svg class="css-uhuo44" height="13" viewbox="0 0 16 13" fill-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></button></div></li><li class="css-60hakz"></li></ul></div></div></li></ul></div></header></div><section class="meteredContent css-1i2y565" itemprop="articleBody" name="articleBody"><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The New York Times and CNN will co-host the next <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/news-event/democratic-debates?module=inline" title="">Democratic debate</a> near Columbus, Ohio, on Oct. 15, with the possibility of a second round one night later depending on how many candidates meet the qualifying criteria. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The Democratic National Committee announced Friday that the debate would be held in Westerville, Ohio, on the campus of Otterbein University. The moderators will be the CNN anchors Anderson Cooper and Erin Burnett as well as The Times’s National editor, Marc Lacey.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">So far 11 candidates have qualified for the CNN/New York Times debate — the 10 Democrats who appeared in <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/12/us/politics/democratic-presidential-debate-recap.html?module=inline" title="">Thursday night’s debate</a> on ABC, as well as the businessman Tom Steyer, who <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/08/us/politics/october-democratic-debate-tom-steyer.html?module=inline" title="">recently qualified for the next one</a>. Other candidates have until the end of the day on Oct. 1 to meet the qualifying standards.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The criteria for October are the same as those for September: Candidates must have 130,000 unique donors and register at least 2 percent support in four qualifying polls.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Steyer, the billionaire investor and impeachment activist, made the cut after a recent CBS News/YouGov poll showed him at 2 percent in Nevada, a key early-voting state.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Along with Mr. Steyer, the October debate will feature:</p><ul class="css-1xx6m9o ez3869y0"><li class="css-o74qhc eoqvrfo0"><p class="css-15hwz5e evys1bk0">Former Vice President <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2020/us/elections/joe-biden.html" title="">Joseph R. Biden Jr.</a></p></li><li class="css-o74qhc eoqvrfo0"><p class="css-15hwz5e evys1bk0">Senator <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2020/us/elections/cory-booker.html" title="">Cory Booker</a> of New Jersey</p></li><li class="css-o74qhc eoqvrfo0"><p class="css-15hwz5e evys1bk0">Mayor <a class="css-1g7m0tk"
